Gutierrez-Negrin L.C.A., Quijano-Leon J.L.	Update of geothermics in Mexico	2004	Geotermia	17	1		21	30		5	http://www.scopus.com/inward/record.url?eid=2-s2.0-4544329397&partnerID=40&md5=c4d3ff4169338304c9504b33e6460186	Comision Federal de Electricidad, A. Volta 655, Morelia 58290, Mexico	Gutiérrez-Negrín, L.C.A., Comision Federal de Electricidad, A. Volta 655, Morelia 58290, Mexico; Quijano-León, J.L., Comision Federal de Electricidad, A. Volta 655, Morelia 58290, Mexico	Four geothermal fields are currently operating in Mexico (Cerro Prieto, Los Azures, Los Humeros and Las Tres Vírgenes), with a total installed geothermal-electric capacity of 953 megawatts(MW). This means the country is located in third place, worldwide, just behind the USA and the Philippines. Thirty-six power plants of several types (condensing, back pressure and binary cycle), between 1.5 and 110 MW, operate in the fields, fed by 197 wells with a combined production of 7,770 metric tons of steam per hour (t/h). These production wells have depths between 600 and 4,400 meters. Steam comes with 8,750 t/h of brine that is injected through 19 injection wells or treated in a solar evaporation pond of 14 km2 in Cerro Prieto. During 2003, steam produced in those fields equalled 67.5 million metric tons, and the power plants generated 6,282 gigawatt-hours (GWh), which represented 3.1% of the electric energy produced in Mexico. All the power plants and the geothermal fields are operated by the public utility, the Comisión Federal de Electricidad (CFE). Arellano G.V.M., Torres R.M.A., Barragan R.R.M., Sandoval M.F.	Response to exploitation (1982-2002) of the Los Azufres, Mich. (Mexico) geothermal field. Part I: North zone [Respuesta a la explotación (1982-2003) del yacimiento geoté rmico de Los Azufres, Mich. (México). Parte I: Zona norte]	2004	Geotermia	17	1		10	20			http://www.scopus.com/inward/record.url?eid=2-s2.0-4544356005&partnerID=40&md5=59aec5ee4168975eab6d4574084d6b21	Inst. de Investigaciones Electricas, Gerencia de Geotermia, Reforma 113, Col. Palmira, 62490 Cuernavaca, Morelos, Mexico; Comision Federal de Electricidad, Residencia Los Azufres, Campamento Agua Fria, Los Azufres, Mexico	Arellano, G.V.M., Inst. de Investigaciones Electricas, Gerencia de Geotermia, Reforma 113, Col. Palmira, 62490 Cuernavaca, Morelos, Mexico; Torres, R.M.A., Comision Federal de Electricidad, Residencia Los Azufres, Campamento Agua Fria, Los Azufres, Mexico; Barragán, R.R.M., Inst. de Investigaciones Electricas, Gerencia de Geotermia, Reforma 113, Col. Palmira, 62490 Cuernavaca, Morelos, Mexico; Sandoval, M.F., Comision Federal de Electricidad, Residencia Los Azufres, Campamento Agua Fria, Los Azufres, Mexico	This work studies the thermodynamic evolution of the Los Azufres northern zone reservoir fluids as a response of exploitation since 1982 to 2002 is presented. Thermodynamic conditions for reservoir fluids were estimated using the WELFLO heat- and flow-well simulator, using production data as the input. The initial thermodynamic conditions of the north zone wells indicated the presence of compressed liquid; also it was noticed that the first response to exploitation was a pressure drop and an enthalpy increase, while the long-term response indicated a very small pressure change but a high enthalphy increment. The analysis of production, chemical and isotopic (δ 18O, δD) data in this zone showed interference effects of fluids reinjected in well Az-52 on well Az-5; and in well Az-15 on wells AZ-13, AZ-28 and Az-43. At the present time due to the low injection flow rates, this effect is minimal. Suarez Arriaga M.C.	Evaluation of the energy potential, biogenesis and essential characteristics of the geothermal submarine systems in Mexico - Northern Mexican coast of the Pacific Ocean and Gulf of California [Evaluación del potencial, biogénesis y caracterí sticas esenciales de los sistemas geotérmicos submarinos en México - Norte de la costa Mexicana del Océano Pací fico y Golfo de California]	2004	Geotermia	17	1		31	44			http://www.scopus.com/inward/record.url?eid=2-s2.0-4544338249&partnerID=40&md5=ab580eb2130f516dc63a927a4b08ef0f	Esc. de Ciencias Fisico-Matematicas, Univ. Michoacana de San Nicolas, Hidalgo, Mexico	Suárez Arriaga, M.C., Esc. de Ciencias Fisico-Matematicas, Univ. Michoacana de San Nicolas, Hidalgo, Mexico	Geothermal energy in Mexico embraces both near-surface traditional reservoirs located between 500 and 3000 meters depth, and deep geothermal resources over 3000 meters in depth. Non-traditional geothermal energy sources in Mexico include the deep portions and boundaries of traditional hydrothermal reservoirs, systems in hot dry or wet rock, geo-pressured reservoirs in the Gulf of Mexico and hydrothermal submarine systems mainly located close to the northern Mexican coast of the Pacific Ocean. Deep submarine energy is related to the existence of hydrothermal vents emerging in many places along the oceanic spreading centers between tectonic plates. These systems have a total length of about 65,000 km in the Earth's oceanic crust. There are two kinds of ocean systems in the Gulf of California: deep resources, located along the rifts between tectonic plates of oceanic crust over 2000 m below sea level, and shallow resources near continental platforms at 20-50 m depth. The shallow, submarine heat is related to faults and fractures in the sea bottom close to some coasts. This type of shallow, sub-sea system is found offshore at Punta Banda in Ensenada, Baja California. The preliminary energy potential of such reservoirs is estimated at an average of 1120 MW t per cubic kilometer of sub-sea rock.. The specific chemical characteristics of the submarine hydrothermal waters found in those systems indicate that water-oceanic rock interactions occur under high-temperature and high-pressure conditions. At the same time, submarine geothermal energy supports rich biological communities at depths where living organisms find no sunlight for photosynthesis. Recent research suggests that possible locations for the synthesis of chemicals needed for the origin of life include submarine hydrothermal systems.
